      <table width="97%" style="margin:auto;">
        <tr>
          <td width="100%">       
            <h1 style="color:#3c8aac;font-weight:bold;">Polysaccharide-Utilization Loci DataBase (PULDB)</h1>
            <strong>PULDB describes <font color="#5CA2A8">Polysaccharide Utilization Loci</font> (PULs) experimentally characterized in the literature, but also
            73,782            PUL predictions in 
            2,227            Bacteroidetes species.</strong><br>
            A PUL is a set of physically-linked genes organized around a <i>susCD gene pair</i>. PULs are prevalent in the Bacteroidetes phylum. They provide an evolutionary advantage to these species by orchestrating the breakdown of complex glycans thanks to the encoded <strong>CAZymes</strong>. Please note that our PUL prediction tool tends to predict more PULs with multiple <i>tandem susCD pairs</i> than what is seen in experimentally determined cases.<br>
          </td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
          <td> 
	    <div class="paragraphe">
              <h3 class="spip">Citing PULDB</h3>
	      <p><b><font color="#980000">A new reference for PULDB ! </font>In the 2018 database issue of <i>Nucleic Acids Research</i>, we summarize the many changes that have occurred in the PULDB during the previous two years.</b><br>
Terrapon N, Lombard V, Drula É, Lapébie P, Al-Masaudi S, Gilbert HJ, Henrissat B (2017) PULDB: the expanded database of Polysaccharide Utilization Loci; <i>Nucleic Acids Research</i> 
	                 <a target="_blank" href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/?term=29088389">Link to the publication</a></p>
	      <p><u>To refer the prediction method</u><br> 
	      Terrapon, N., Lombard, V., Gilbert, H.J. and Henrissat, B. (2015) Automatic prediction of polysaccharide utilization loci in Bacteroidetes species from the human gut microbiota; <i>Bioinformatics</i> 31(5):647-55 - 
              <a target="_blank" href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/?term=25355788">Link to the publication</a></p>
            </div>
          </td>
        </tr>
      </table>
